## Parliamentary elections 19 April 2026 — national summary

Turnout: 50.70% (3,360,330 of 6,627,747 registered).
Biggest gain: ПрБ (+44.59 pp). Biggest loss: ГЕРБ-СДС (-13.00 pp).
Paper / machine vote: 52.39% / 47.61%.
Section-level anomalies detected: 3,331 (recount: 0; machine flash removed: 3,077; problem sections: 138).

## Parties — retrospective analysis

Analysis of each party that cleared the threshold on 19 April 2026 — what worked, what did not, and strategic notes for the next vote.

### ПП ИМА ТАКЪВ НАРОД (ИТН)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%98%D0%A2%D0%9D

## Headline result

ITN (Има Такъв Народ / There Is Such a People) took 23,861 votes (0.74%) from eleventh place — down from 6.78% in October 2024 (7th position), a -6.05pp loss and -141,330 absolute votes. Slavi Trifonov's party fell out of parliament and is politically marginal.

## What worked

- Weak but even geography — top-5 regions hold only 31.49% of the vote, meaning the party doesn't depend on a single source.
- Abroad over-index 1.17 — the diaspora stayed close.
- 4 ballot-order upsets — Slavi Trifonov is no longer the automatic leader everywhere. Hristinka Ivanova in Pleven (421 prefs) beat the local central names.

## What didn't work

- 0.74% — effectively the end of the party. Zero state subsidy, zero parliamentary presence.
- A -6.05pp loss across all regions evenly — Pleven -6.20, Ruse -6.02, Plovdiv -5.49, Razgrad, Targovishte. Systemic disintegration.
- Risk-section share — 0.75% (over-index 1.02), compared to 7.45% in October 2024 — a -6.70pp drop. ITN lost this base too.
- Against ACB (closest rival): 28 of 32 won — so ITN is still larger than the other micro-parties, but out of parliament.

## Geographic strategy

For a party at 0.74%, geographic strategy does not exist. The strategy is survival — preserving the structure for the next cycle or merging.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 0.75% at over-index 1.02 — close to national, but absolute votes are under 250 across the whole network. Not material.

## Candidates and preferences

10,323 preferences, rate 43.26% (high for a falling party — a loyal remnant). Top-1 4.08%. Hristinka Ivanova leads in Pleven (421), Slavi Trifonov in 25-MIR (380), Stanislav Balabanov in Plovdiv (335). 4 ballot-order upsets — Trifonov is losing as the central name.

## Competitive geography

Against ACB: 28 won, 4 lost. Top margins: Vidin +0.90pp, Kyustendil +0.62. Losses: 23-MIR -0.53, 24-MIR -0.34. ITN leads in small towns against the new micro-parties but is invisible in Sofia.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Decision on continuation or wind-down.** At 0.74% and -6pp collapse, the campaign may not be viable. Leadership must decide.
- **Merger with another residual party.** ITN + Siyanie or ITN + ACB — arithmetically insufficient to clear the threshold, but cheaper than a standalone structure.
- **Protect the local names.** Ivanova, Balabanov — they preserved their own vote and can be assets for a new formation.
- **Do not rely on Slavi Trifonov.** The historic 25-30% from 2021 will not return. New identity or end.

### АЛИАНС ЗА ПРАВА И СВОБОДИ – АПС (АПС)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%90%D0%9F%D0%A1

## Headline result

APS (Alliance for Rights and Freedoms) took 50,759 votes (1.57%) from tenth place — far below the 4% threshold. After the DPS split between Delyan Peevski and the Doğan faction in 2024, APS was the political home of the post-Doğan wing. The result is catastrophic: the Turkish minority APS hoped to consolidate transferred to PB.

## What worked

- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 2.40 — structurally, APS remained a Turkish-minority party. 43.93% of the party vote comes from those 8 oblasts.
- Abroad over-index 2.36 — the Turkish-origin diaspora stayed close.
- 12 ballot-order upsets out of 30 — the post-DPS local networks function: Ahmed Vranchev in Blagoevgrad (621 prefs), Esra Ibish in Haskovo (446), Sevim Ali in Burgas (327). Local Turkish-community representatives have their own vote.
- Against ITN (closest rival in vote total): 18 of 32 won — losing side of the parliamentary market, winning side of its own segment.

## What didn't work

- 1.57% — failure. APS did not inherit a single point of DPS's 19% from October 2024.
- Collapse in traditional Turkish oblasts: Kardzhali -32.97pp (4.27% for APS vs 56% for DPS), Razgrad -32.11pp (5.24%), Silistra -18.13pp (6.00%). The community did not follow Doğan.
- Risk-section share — 2.13% (over-index 1.36, vs 12.21% for DPS before). A small residue.
- Sofia City over-index 0.11 — essentially zero in the capital. APS does not exist outside its specific ethnic segment.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** Targovishte and Silistra — the only places with positive margins over ITN. **Rebuild** Kardzhali and Razgrad — but against DPS-Peevski on one side and PB on the other, resources required are enormous.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 2.13% in the 138 sections at over-index 1.36 — above proportional, but absolute votes are small. Not a road to parliament.

## Candidates and preferences

12,745 preferences, rate 25.11%, top-1 4.87%. Ahmed Vranchev leads in Blagoevgrad (621), Esra Ibish in Haskovo (446), Sevim Ali in Burgas (327). 12 ballot-order upsets — APS's central list has no mobilising power; local regional names are the principal asset.

## Competitive geography

Against ITN: 18 won, 14 lost. Top margins: Targovishte +6.09pp, Silistra +5.42. Losses: Vidin -0.94, Pleven -0.71. The real competitor for this base, however, is not ITN — it is DPS-Peevski (for residual Turkish loyalty) and PB (for everyone who wanted change).

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Negotiate unification with DPS-Peevski.** APS + DPS = ~9% — back to parliamentary weight. Standalone, both under 8%.
- **Promote the local winners.** Vranchev, Ibish, Ali — they have an electorate; the central list does not.
- **Acknowledge the bloc loss.** The Turkish minority voted for PB. The next campaign cannot take this base for granted.
- **Concentrate resources in Targovishte and Silistra.** The only regions where APS leads in a standalone view.

### АНТИКОРУПЦИОНЕН БЛОК (АКБ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%90%D0%9A%D0%91

## Headline result

ACB (Anti-Corruption Bloc) took 18,999 votes (0.59%) from twelfth place in its ballot debut. The party did not exist in October 2024; for a debut formation under a new identity, the result is symbolic — no parliament, but a political brand declared.

## What worked

- Sofia City over-index 1.76 — the strongest urban identity after PB and PP-DB. 33.70% of the party vote comes from the three Sofia MIRs.
- Other big cities over-index 1.16 — Varna, Plovdiv, Burgas accept the brand.
- Toma Belev (known environmentalist and political activist) is the face: 474 preferences in 23-MIR, 4 ballot-order upsets. For a debut, a real bench with its own identity.
- Against BB (closest rival): 23 of 32 won.

## What didn't work

- 0.59% — far from 4%. For a party with debut urban ambition, this is below potential.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.49 — no connection to minority communities.
- Abroad over-index 1.07 — close to proportional, but absolute numbers are negligible.
- Lost 9 regions to BB, all in north-west and central Bulgaria. The party is purely Sofia-based.

## Geographic strategy

For a party with debut 0.59% and an urban core, the geographic strategy is concentration. **Defend** Sofia City and Plovdiv, where over-indexes 1.76 and 1.16 show real brand presence. **Ignore** everything else — wasting resources on a national campaign at this level is a loss.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 0.57% at over-index 0.97 — almost no presence. Expected for an anti-corruption urban platform.

## Candidates and preferences

7,443 preferences, rate 39.18%, top-1 6.37%. Toma Belev in 23-MIR (474), Vasil Gyurov in 23-MIR (209), Konstantin Bachiyski in Burgas (203). 4 ballot-order upsets — for a debut party, good local pull.

## Competitive geography

Against BB: 23 won, 9 lost. Top margins: Burgas +0.25pp, Abroad +0.21. Losses: Pernik -0.88, 24-MIR -0.44. Competition is between micro-parties and does not determine parliamentary chances.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Negotiate unification with Siyanie, BC or BB.** Four new urban parties split the same ~5% electorate. One merged could clear the threshold.
- **Develop Toma Belev as the principal face.** 4 upsets and own pull in 23-MIR — foundation for the next campaign.
- **Focus exclusively on cities.** Over-index 1.76 in Sofia and 1.16 in big cities — that is where the return is.
- **Don't build a national structure.** At 0.59%, regional branches are cost without revenue. Digital campaign, focused on urban identity.

### ПП ВЕЛИЧИЕ (Величие)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%B5

## Headline result

Velichie took 100,572 votes (3.10%) from seventh place — down from 4.00% in October 2024 (9th position). Better positioning, no parliament. Minimal loss of -0.90pp at +3,075 absolute votes — the party absorbed part of the turnout increase but not enough to clear 4%.

## What worked

- Climbed from 9th to 7th as competitors contracted (Vazrazhdane collapsed).
- Abroad over-index 1.86 — one of the strongest diaspora over-indexes. 10.73% of the national vote comes from abroad.
- Mild gains in small central and western regions: Pazardzhik +0.89pp, Lovech +0.85, Gabrovo +0.75, Targovishte +0.68, Kyustendil +0.66 — local-niche progress.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster +0.22pp — the only positive there, against the trend. Small but exceptional.
- Yuliana Mateeva in Varna (5.28% of national prefs) and Ivelin Mihaylov in 25-MIR (4.25%) — two local names with their own draw.

## What didn't work

- Did not cross 4%. Sixth or seventh result in a row below the threshold — systemic wall, not bad campaign.
- Losses in big cities and Sofia MIRs: Varna -0.57pp, 25-MIR -0.17, Plovdiv -0.15, 23-MIR -0.15. The party does not break the urban liberal wall.
- Pollsters underestimated Velichie by 0.20 to 1.40pp (TR -1.40, GIB -1.16); only ML over-polled (+0.55). An under-poll for a threshold-edge party means the campaign worked in panic mode.
- Against BSP-UL (closest rival in vote total): 14 of 32 won, 18 lost — the losing side.
- Only 1 ballot-order upset — central list strong, bench thin outside Mihaylov.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** abroad — the only field with double-digit over-indexing. **Attack** in small central and western regions (Lovech, Gabrovo, Kyustendil) where deltas are positive. **Concede** big cities and Sofia MIRs — the party has no urban draw.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 3.27% at over-index 1.05 — close to national. Maksuda 4.22%, Stolipinovo 2.76%, Dolno Ezerovo 4.21%. Small drop vs October 2024 (-0.97pp). Same as MECh — these sections deliver under 1,000 votes for the party. Not a road to 4%.

## Candidates and preferences

34,447 preferences, rate 34.25%, top-1 5.28%. Yuliana Mateeva leads in Varna (1,820), Ivelin Mihaylov in 25-MIR (1,465), Pavel Stoimenov in Blagoevgrad (1,224), Yordan Mitsikulev in Pazardzhik (1,102), Krasimira Ninova-Katincharova in Stara Zagora (1,024). Only 1 ballot-order upset — Mihail Dinev beat Ljubisha Blazhevski in Burgas. Central list dominates.

## Competitive geography

Against BSP-UL (closest rival): won 14, lost 18. Top margins: Abroad +4.84pp, Varna +1.92, Veliko Tarnovo +1.19. Losses: Yambol -2.60, Kyustendil -1.64, Sofia region -1.43. The two parties split the same pool, but BSP-UL has a wider small-town base.

## Polling intelligence

Six of seven agencies underestimated Velichie: AR -0.20pp, CAM -0.58, MY -0.90, SH -1.00, GIB -1.16, TR -1.40 — only ML over-polled (+0.55). Systematic ~1pp under-poll — the party took 1pp more than market expectations. A small buffer against the threshold, but too small to clear it.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Negotiate a coalition with MECh.** MECh + Velichie = 6.33% — over the threshold. Standalone, both under 4%.
- **Defend abroad.** Over-index 1.86 is the party's asset. A diaspora-focused campaign could deliver +0.3pp nationally.
- **Develop Mihaylov and Mateeva.** Two faces with over 1,400 prefs each — they can become visible leadership in the campaign.
- **Quit the urban contest.** Over-index 0.70 in Sofia City at +12pp turnout growth — impossible to break through.
- **Reallocate to small central regions.** Positive deltas in Lovech, Gabrovo, Kyustendil show where the return is.

### ГЕРБ-СДС

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%93%D0%95%D0%A0%D0%91-%D0%A1%D0%94%D0%A1

## Headline result

GERB-SDS took 433,755 votes (13.39%), placing a distant second behind PB (Progressive Bulgaria), which swept the election with 44.59% — half GERB-SDS's October 2024 share (26.39%, position 1). The collapse is starker against turnout: with the electorate expanding from 38.81% to 50.70% (+11.89pp), the party still shed 208,766 absolute votes. Every new voter who showed up on April 19 went to PB — the entire turnout surge was absorbed by the winner.

## What worked

- Held the regional leaders in the central-west (Lovech, Montana, Vratsa) — leads of 11-14pp over PP-DB in areas where the urban liberal opposition has no organisational depth.
- Preference engagement was high (51.26% of voters cast a preferential vote), suggesting a list-loyal core that still showed up.
- Stronghold concentration is moderate (top-5 regions = 32.44% of national vote), so the loss is not concentrated in any single geography.
- Local figures over-performed central names in 13 of roughly 30 regions — Stefan Apostolov in Blagoevgrad (6,860 prefs, beating Rosen Zhelyazkov by over 4,400), Gyunay Hyusmen in Razgrad (2,327 vs 306 for the list leader), Georgi Stankov in Haskovo (5,606 vs Delyan Dobrev's 2,991). The bench is real.

## What didn't work

- Lost 208,766 absolute votes in a +12pp turnout election — the worst possible combination.
- The other three big cities (Varna, Plovdiv, Burgas) shed 8.40pp of vote share collectively. Urban erosion is structural, not a one-region story.
- Risk-neighborhood vote share fell from 36.12% to 11.41% — a 24.71pp drop. GERB-SDS's traditional capacity to mobilise these sections has evaporated.
- Steep losses in the southern core: Vratsa -11.58pp, Dobrich -11.55pp, Smolyan -10.66pp, Haskovo -10.65pp, Lovech -9.70pp.
- Pollsters missed the collapse: every published agency over-polled GERB-SDS by 5-11pp, with GIB at +11.21pp and CAM at +10.93pp. The party walked into election night expecting a much better result.

## Geographic strategy

GERB-SDS is now an outside-the-big-cities party in everything but name. Sofia City delivered 13.25% (-4.56pp), and the Sofia-Plovdiv-Varna-Burgas axis combined gives the party 18.89% of its national total against 22.27% prior. **Defend** the central-west belt (Lovech, Montana, Vratsa, Blagoevgrad) where margins over PP-DB remain double-digit. **Attack** the smaller mixed-population oblasts (Razgrad, Shumen, Kardzhali) where the -6.80pp ethnic-mixed cluster delta is recoverable through local figures already proven at the polls. **Triage** the three Sofia constituencies and abroad — losing margins of -19pp to -3pp; recovery there needs a different list and message, not an incremental fix.

## Risk neighborhoods

The collapse here is the single most striking number in the bundle: 36.12% → 11.41% share of votes cast in monitored Roma-neighborhood sections, an over-index ratio of 0.85 (now slightly below the party's national share). Stolipinovo (71 sections, Plovdiv) gave 10.87%, Maksuda (26 sections, Varna) 12.11%, Pobeda (Burgas) the highest at 22.95%. Whatever ground operation produced 36% in October 2024 was either dismantled or out-organised by competitors.

## Candidates and preferences

Half the party's voters used a preferential vote (51.26% — one of the highest engagement rates in the field). The top single candidate nationally is Boyko Borisov at 7,063 votes in 25-MIR Sofia, but only 3.18% of all party prefs — striking dispersion. The list of local figures beating the central name is long: Stefan Apostolov (Blagoevgrad), Gyunay Hyusmen (Razgrad), Georgi Stankov (Haskovo), Martin Harizanov (Vratsa), Irena Dimova (Montana). 13 ballot-order upsets across roughly 30 regions tell a clear story: GERB-SDS is a federation of regional brands, not a Borisov-monolith party. The list strategy has to acknowledge this.

## Competitive geography

Against PP-DB — the closest national rival in vote total — GERB-SDS won 26 regions to 6 lost. But the six losses are the demographically decisive ones: Sofia 23, 24, 25 (-19, -13, -4pp), Plovdiv-city and abroad. Suburbanisation and youth turnout will keep pushing these regions further; the party cannot win a national plurality through the central-west belt alone.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies over-polled GERB-SDS: MY +5.11pp, TR +5.71, AR +6.11, SH +6.21, ML +7.79, CAM +10.93, GIB +11.21. CAM and GIB were the largest misses; the late-fieldwork agencies (MY 6d, TR 3d, AR 4d) clustered at +5-6pp. Historical bias is mildly positive across the board for GERB-SDS (TR +0.99, SH +1.08, AR +1.26, ML +1.47, GIB +1.84 over multiple cycles), but this cycle's overestimate is roughly 4× the long-run pattern. The campaign was almost certainly making decisions with a 19-21% target in mind.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Treat April 2026 as a regime break, not a swing.** Losing 13pp in one cycle while turnout rose 12pp is structural, not tactical.
- **Rebuild the risk-neighborhood ground operation from scratch.** The 24.71pp collapse in those sections is the single biggest leakage and the cheapest to address with field investment.
- **Reorder the lists around proven local figures.** The 13 ballot-order upsets are a free roadmap — lead with Apostolov in Blagoevgrad, Hyusmen in Razgrad, Stankov in Haskovo, Dimova in Montana.
- **Don't trust the polls.** Build internal tracking that adjusts for the 5-11pp systemic over-polling exposed in this cycle, or the next campaign will misallocate resources again.
- **Concede the urban liberal vote and pivot.** Sofia 23/24/25, Plovdiv-city and abroad are now competitive only with a different message — don't waste a national campaign chasing them at the expense of the central-west belt.

### Движение за права и свободи - ДПС (ДПС)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%94%D0%9F%D0%A1

## Headline result

DPS took 230,693 votes (7.12%) and dropped to fourth — down from 19% in October 2024, a -11.88pp loss and -231,807 absolute votes. Delyan Peevski's party held Kardzhali (56.16%) and Targovishte but lost almost everywhere else in its historically resilient ethnic-mixed base. Votes DPS had held for decades transferred to PB.

## What worked

- Kardzhali stayed a fortress: 56.16% and a +54.87pp lead over closest rival Vazrazhdane. The Turkish-minority vote held.
- The ethnic-mixed cluster stayed proportionally over-indexed: over-index 2.91, share 20.69%, contributing 53.16% of the party's national vote. The structural geography is intact, just shrunk.
- 24 ballot-order upsets out of 30 — exceptional local decentralisation of the vote. Fatima Yaldas beat Delyan Peevski in Blagoevgrad (1,291 vs 462), Ismail Osman beat Kalin Stoyanov in Burgas, Aysel Mustafova crushed Nida Ahmedov in Shumen (1,568 vs 339). Local notables hold their own electorate independently of the central list.
- Paper voting at 86.61% — second-highest in the field, marker of a loyal older / rural electorate.

## What didn't work

- Losses across traditional fortresses: Razgrad -24.39pp, Kardzhali -20.92pp, Targovishte -20.74pp, Silistra -14.46pp, Shumen. An entire belt eroded.
- Abroad -16.68pp — the diaspora did not follow.
- Risk-section share fell from 12.21% to 2.35% (-9.86pp) — over-index 0.33, now under-indexed. PB took this base at 50%+.
- Pollsters systematically overestimated the party: CAM +6.90pp, GIB +4.10, TR +3.08, SH +2.88. The campaign almost certainly worked with a 9-12% target.
- 24 ballot-order upsets — flipped — also mean the central list (i.e. Peevski) has no mobilising power outside specific municipalities.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** Kardzhali and Targovishte — the only places with double-digit leads over rivals. **Rebuild** Razgrad, Silistra, Shumen — where PB or others took votes DPS had held for decades. **Concede** the cities and abroad — over-indexes of 0.11 in Sofia and 0.51 in big cities mean the party simply doesn't exist as an urban option.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share in the 138 monitored sections fell from 12.21% to 2.35%, a -9.86pp drop — over-index 0.33, meaning DPS took less than a third of its national share in those sections. Stolipinovo 1.80%, Pobeda (Burgas) 10.86%, Filipovci 8.95%. Whatever organisational presence existed in Roma neighborhoods has collapsed. PB took the bloc at 50%+.

## Candidates and preferences

70,766 preferential votes, rate 30.68%, top-1 share only 2.26% — extreme dispersion. 24 ballot-order upsets — more than any other party. DPS's local networks function; the central list does not. Most telling: Fatima Yaldas (Blagoevgrad, 1,291 prefs) beat Delyan Peevski (462) — the party leader lost his own district to a regional figure. Aysel Mustafova in Shumen took 1,568 vs 339 for Nida Ahmedov. Vasil Petkov in Pleven took 1,018 vs 419 for Dimitar Avramov. The party is a federation of regional brokers; Peevski is the name on the ballot, not a vote driver.

## Competitive geography

Against Vazrazhdane (closest rival in vote total): won 21 of 32, lost 11. Top margins: Kardzhali +54.87pp, Targovishte +22.02, Razgrad +16.75. Losses: Gabrovo -4.42, 25-MIR -4.18, 23-MIR -3.95 — Sofia and the north are unfamiliar terrain for DPS. The real competitor for this base, however, is not Vazrazhdane — it is PB.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies overestimated DPS. Errors: ML +0.53pp, MY +1.98, AR +2.28, SH +2.88, TR +3.08, GIB +4.10, CAM +6.90. Systematic ~3pp overestimate across the field, with CAM and GIB at over +4pp. The campaign entered election day expecting 9-12% and double the mandate count. Reality was different.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Acknowledge the loss of the Roma bloc as final.** -9.86pp in risk sections and the 12.21%-to-2.35% collapse mean the network is dismantled. Quick recovery will cost more than investment in a new identity.
- **Promote the local winners.** Yaldas, Mustafova, Osman, Petkov — they belong at the top of next cycle's lists. They have an electorate; Peevski has less every cycle.
- **Defend Kardzhali with a local, not central, campaign.** The +54.87pp lead is a buffer, but Turkey and local Muslim leaders remain active — not to be taken for granted.
- **Distrust the polls.** Systematic 3pp overestimate — next time, mark everything down.
- **Consider a coalition with the DPS family.** APS took 1.57% standalone. A combined list would land at 9-10% — back to parliamentary weight.

### БЪЛГАРИЯ МОЖЕ (БМ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%91%D0%9C

## Headline result

BC (Bulgaria Can) took 17,263 votes (0.53%) from fourteenth place in its ballot debut — the last party above 0.5%. For a debut formation the result is symbolic; there is no standalone political future.

## What worked

- Sofia City over-index 1.71 — an urban profile typical for a new city party. 32.58% of the party vote comes from the three Sofia MIRs.
- Other big cities over-index 1.11 — Varna, Plovdiv, Burgas accept the brand modestly.
- Kuzman Iliev (known economist and media voice) is the face: 678 prefs in 25-MIR, 633 in Varna. For a debut — a real leader's pull.
- Against BB (closest rival): 17 of 32 won — near-tie in the micro-party field.

## What didn't work

- 0.53% — barely above the registration threshold. No parliament, no state subsidy, no structural future.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.47 — no breakthrough.
- Losses in north-western regions: Pernik -0.93pp vs BB, 24-MIR -0.60. Even in pure competition with other micro-parties, doesn't win.
- Only 2 ballot-order upsets — the central list is strong, but the bench is thin outside Iliev.

## Geographic strategy

For a party at 0.53% with an urban core, the geographic strategy is concentration. **Defend** Sofia City and Varna, where over-indexes are highest. **Ignore** everything else.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 0.59% at over-index 1.11 — close to proportional, but absolute numbers are negligible.

## Candidates and preferences

5,472 preferences, rate 31.70%, top-1 12.39% — concentrated central list around Iliev. Kuzman Iliev in 25-MIR (678) and Varna (633), Aleksandar Marinov in 23-MIR (353). 2 ballot-order upsets.

## Competitive geography

Against BB: 17 won, 15 lost — near-tie. Top margins: Abroad +0.18pp, Veliko Tarnovo +0.18. Losses: Pernik -0.93, 24-MIR -0.60. Micro-parties compete for the same droplet electorate.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Merge with ACB, Siyanie, BB.** Four new micro-parties with similar urban profiles compete for a ~5% combined electorate. One unified platform is the only path above 4%.
- **Develop Iliev as a leadership figure.** Top-1 12.39% means the central list works — but absolutely it is under 700 prefs, so mobilising weight is low.
- **Don't build a national structure.** Digital campaign, focused on Sofia-Varna-Plovdiv, with resources commensurate with 0.5%.
- **Acknowledge the debut floor.** For a party with no history, 0.53% is a starting point, not an end. The next campaign must position between PB and PP-DB — inaccessible territory, but better than disappearance.

### СИЯНИЕ (Сияние)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5

## Headline result

Siyanie took 93,559 votes (2.89%) from ninth place in its ballot debut — just below the 4% threshold, no parliament. The party did not exist in October 2024; for a debut campaign this is a notable result but insufficient.

## What worked

- For a debut — almost the threshold. Only 1.11pp separates the party from a parliamentary seat; the next campaign starts with recognition, not from zero.
- Sofia City over-index 1.56 — an urban profile typical for a new urban-protest party. 29.75% of the party vote comes from the three Sofia MIRs.
- Other big cities over-index 1.27 — Varna, Plovdiv-city, Burgas accept the brand.
- Nikolay Popov leads in two MIRs: 23-MIR Sofia (3,965) and 25-MIR Sofia (2,772). A recognisable face with his own draw. Top-1 share 13.82% — central list, but not catastrophically concentrated.
- Against BSP-UL (closest rival): won 8 of 32, lost 24 — losing side, but not a rout.

## What didn't work

- Did not cross 4%. For a party with real urban backing, that is the key task for the next cycle.
- Weak periphery: Yambol -3.81pp (vs BSP-UL), Dobrich -2.40. Outside the cities — almost nothing.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.48 — no breakthrough to minority communities.
- Abroad over-index 0.71 — the diaspora does not engage with a debut urban party.
- Only 1 ballot-order upset — the central list is strong, but the bench is thin outside Popov.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** Sofia City and Plovdiv where the party leads or is close to leading. **Build** in small central regions through local candidates — current geography is concentrated in 5 regions (44.73% of national vote).

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 3.30% at over-index 1.14 — slightly above proportional. Small base, not a priority.

## Candidates and preferences

28,699 preferences, rate 30.67%, top-1 13.82% — Nikolay Popov is the face of the brand. In Varna, Simeon Trulev (1,381). 1 ballot-order upset — the central list dominates.

## Competitive geography

Against BSP-UL: 8 won, 24 lost. Top margins: 25-MIR +1.75pp, Plovdiv +1.65. Losses: Yambol -3.81, Dobrich -2.40. The two parties compete for differently-shaped electorates — Siyanie is urban, BSP-UL is small-town.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Cross 4%.** For a debut party at 2.89% with an urban core, +1.5pp in Sofia and Plovdiv is a realistic target.
- **Build a bench beyond Popov.** 1 upset means nobody but the leader brings their own vote.
- **Don't waste resources in rural regions.** Over-indexes 0.48-0.71 in rural and diaspora regions — negative ROI.
- **Prepare for coalition or merger with a similar new party.** Siyanie + ACB + BC = ~4% from a pure urban base.

### ПРОГРЕСИВНА БЪЛГАРИЯ (ПрБ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%91

## Headline result

PB (Progressive Bulgaria) took 1,444,920 votes (44.59%) on its first appearance on the ballot, swept all 32 multi-member districts, and lapped second-place GERB-SDS (13.39%) by 31pp. Turnout surged from 38.81% to 50.70% (+11.89pp), and effectively the entire incremental electorate consolidated behind PB — ex-president Rumen Radev's vehicle.

## What worked

- A 32-for-32 regional sweep with leads of 19-45pp over GERB-SDS. The smallest margin (Kardzhali +19.48pp) is larger than the entire GERB-SDS-to-PP-DB gap.
- Geographic distribution is unusually flat: top-5 regions hold only 28.10% of the national vote and top-25 municipalities 45.13%. PB is broadly mobilised, not stronghold-driven.
- Won 50.46% of votes in monitored Roma-neighborhood sections — over-index 1.13 — including 50.48% in Stolipinovo (71 sections, Plovdiv) and 60.12% in Dolno Ezerovo (Burgas). The bloc GERB-SDS held with 36% in October 2024 transferred wholesale.
- Half a million preferential votes (522,478, prefRate 36.16%). The top candidate — Radev in Burgas — captured only 4.35% of national prefs. The bench is broad: Galab Donev (Pazardzhik), Ilin Dimitrov (Varna), Vladimir Nikolov (Plovdiv), Aleksandar Pulev (Stara Zagora), Encho Keryazov (Yambol).
- Pollsters underestimated by 4-15pp across all seven agencies — competitors planned against a much smaller PB.

## What didn't work

For a debut sweep, "didn't work" is a thin category. The structural weaknesses:

- Sofia City under-indexed at 0.81 — won, but proportionally weaker than the national average. The three Sofia constituencies returned 32-35% versus 44.59% nationally.
- Abroad under-indexed at 0.85 — diaspora communication channels were thinner than domestic ones.
- Kardzhali the only oblast where PB placed second (24.33%, behind DPS at 47%+) — the Turkish-minority vote held against the wave.
- Only 3 ballot-order upsets out of 30 — the central list dominated almost everywhere, which is partly a strength but also means few local figures have built their own electorate beyond Radev.

## Geographic strategy

The party won everywhere; the question is where to consolidate and where the lead is fragile. **Defend** the central-north and north-east ring where margins over GERB-SDS exceed 38pp (Yambol, prov. Plovdiv, Veliko Tarnovo, Pleven, Dobrich). **Watch** Sofia City — under-indexed at 0.81 and PP-DB, not GERB-SDS, is the closest rival there, a different competitive dynamic. **Build** in Kardzhali (the only loss) and across the ethnic-mixed cluster broadly: PB took 40.89%, over-index 0.92 — the brand is acceptable but not dominant.

## Risk neighborhoods

PB took 50.46% of votes in the 138 monitored Roma-neighborhood sections — over-index 1.13, the highest of any party in the field. Stolipinovo (71 sections, Plovdiv) gave 50.48%, Maksuda (26 sections, Varna) 49.44%, Dolno Ezerovo (Burgas) 60.12%, Fakulteta (Sofia) 53.73%. GERB-SDS held this bloc with a 36% national share; it transferred almost cleanly. Whoever ran the field operation deserves credit — and ought to be retained.

## Candidates and preferences

Half a million preferential votes (522,478, prefRate 36.16%). The top candidate — Rumen Radev — took only 4.35% of national prefs because his votes split across two MIRs: 22,741 in Burgas (58.41% of regional prefs) and 21,541 in 25-MIR Sofia (75.78%). Beyond Radev the list draws on recognisable figures: Galab Donev (Pazardzhik), Ilin Dimitrov (Varna), Vladimir Nikolov (Plovdiv), Aleksandar Pulev (Stara Zagora), Encho Keryazov (Yambol). Only 3 ballot-order upsets out of 30 — the central list held almost everywhere, which is both strength (discipline) and weakness (thin bench outside Radev and the presidential circle).

## Competitive geography

There is no real competitive contest in 2026. Against the closest rival GERB-SDS, PB won 32 of 32 regions with margins from +19.48pp (Kardzhali) to +45.25pp (Yambol). The narrowest leads — Kardzhali, Blagoevgrad (+20pp), 23-MIR Sofia (+20pp), 24-MIR Sofia (+22pp), Lovech (+27pp) — define where the next cycle's competitive map will form. None is currently lose-able, but PP-DB is the structural challenger in Sofia City; GERB-SDS or a rebuilt centre-right is the challenger in the central-west.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies under-polled PB — by between 4.46pp (CAM) and 14.71pp (GIB). ML -8.36, SH -9.89, MY -9.99, AR -10.39, TR -11.39. Even the latest-fieldwork agencies (ML 3d, TR 3d, AR 4d) missed by 8-11pp. With no historical comparison (debut cycle), the cycle's bias is the entire picture. The systematic under-poll is the mirror image of GERB-SDS's over-poll: every published agency's model failed to capture either the PB wave or the new voters it brought in.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Do not read this as a baseline.** 44.59% at debut against a fragmented field with a halo candidate is a ceiling condition, not a floor. Expect normalisation toward the high 20s / low 30s in the next cycle if Radev does not lead.
- **Build the post-Radev bench now.** Top-1 share of 4.35% is structurally healthy, but only 3 ballot-order upsets means few local figures have built their own electorate. Two cycles from now this will matter.
- **Invest in Sofia City and the diaspora.** Both under-indexed at ~0.85; they are the missing piece of a true national majority and the most contested by PP-DB.
- **Hold the risk-neighborhood field operation.** A 50.46% share is the largest single-cycle bloc transfer in recent BG politics — the operation that delivered it is institutional capital, not an artifact of the wave.
- **Manage the polling environment.** A 4-15pp under-poll across every agency in the debut cycle means the campaign was operating with a distorted picture of its own support; private tracking with safety margins is a one-cycle priority.

### СИНЯ БЪЛГАРИЯ (СБ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%A1%D0%91

## Headline result

BB (Blue Bulgaria) took 18,640 votes (0.58%) from thirteenth place — down from 1.07% in October 2024, a -0.49pp loss and -7,405 absolute votes. Petar Moskov's party preserved its identity but lost a quarter of an already minimal electorate.

## What worked

- Sofia City over-index 2.21 — the strongest urban-conservative identity in the field. 42.15% of the party vote comes from the three Sofia MIRs.
- Mild gains in minority regions: Targovishte +0.14pp, Kardzhali +0.13 — atypical direction, likely a consequence of competitor collapse.
- 6 ballot-order upsets — Vili Lilkov (820 prefs in 23-MIR) and Petar Moskov (675 in 24-MIR, 386 in Varna) are recognisable faces. Top-1 share 10.63% — concentrated central list.
- Preference rate 41.39% — high for such a small party, a loyal remnant.

## What didn't work

- 0.58% — near-zero weight. The party is essentially off the electoral radar.
- Losses in Sofia MIRs: 23-MIR -0.69pp, 24-MIR -0.60. Even in its own stronghold, BB is losing share.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.43 — no breakthrough.
- Against ACB (closest rival): 9 of 32 won, 23 lost — losing side against new urban competition.
- Abroad over-index 0.73 — the diaspora does not recognise the brand.

## Geographic strategy

For a party at 0.58%, geographic strategy is impossible. **Defend** the Sofia MIRs if realistic. **Acknowledge** that BB cannot be a standalone force.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 0.53% at over-index 0.92 — close to national, but absolute numbers are negligible.

## Candidates and preferences

7,716 preferences, rate 41.39%, top-1 10.63%. Vili Lilkov leads in 23-MIR (820), Petar Moskov in 24-MIR (675) and Varna (386). 6 ballot-order upsets — high concentration around two leaders and a handful of locals.

## Competitive geography

Against ACB: 9 won, 23 lost. Top margins: Pernik +0.88pp, 24-MIR +0.44. Losses: Burgas -0.25, Abroad -0.20. ACB — new, no history, similar urban profile — beats BB almost everywhere. A signal of an expired brand.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Merge with ACB or BC.** Three parties with similar socio-liberal profiles compete for the same sub-1% electorate. A meaningful coalition is the only path.
- **Develop Moskov and Lilkov as platforms.** They have their own vote; the party brand does not.
- **Acknowledge the position.** BB was the centre-right party of the 2010s. In 2026 that electorate is at PP-DB or PB. New identity or shutdown.

### ПП МЕЧ (МЕЧ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%9C%D0%95%D0%A7

## Headline result

MECh took 104,506 votes (3.23%) and stayed below the 4% threshold from sixth place — down from 4.60% in October 2024 (8th position). Better positioning, still no parliament. A -1.37pp loss and -7,487 votes in a +12pp turnout election — essentially flat numbers in a contracting sectorally non-competitive market.

## What worked

- The party climbed from 8th to 6th — fragmentation of the national-conservative vote (Vazrazhdane collapsed) gave MECh room to absorb part of it.
- Over-index 1.35 in risk neighborhoods — the only "competitive" party with notable over-indexing in those sections. Fakulteta (Sofia) gave 11.93%.
- Mild gains in north-west Bulgaria: Pleven +0.62pp, Vidin +0.55, Pernik +0.43, Montana +0.36 — a belt where GERB-SDS is the historical strong player and is now eroding.
- Pollsters were almost exact: errors from -0.88 to +0.47pp. No election-day surprise.
- Radostin Vasilev (former Sofia mayoral candidate) is a recognisable face: 6.58% of national prefs — top-1 concentration, but not dominating.

## What didn't work

- Did not cross 4%. Without parliamentary weight, the next campaign starts at zero state subsidy.
- Against Velichie (closest rival): 17 of 32 regions won, 15 lost — essentially a tie. The two parties compete for the same electorate but neither wins.
- Only 1 ballot-order upset out of 30 — the central list is strong, but the bench is shallow. Outside Radostin Vasilev there is no independent draw.
- Weak ethnic-mixed cluster: over-index 0.63, share 2.04%. The party has no bridge.
- Concentration around strongholds: Stara Zagora -0.89pp, Silistra -0.83, Haskovo -1.03, Sliven -1.05 — drop in the south-east.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** the north-west where growth is real (Pleven, Vidin, Pernik, Montana). **Attack** the south-east (Sliven, Silistra, Haskovo), where the party is losing share and needs local figures. **Concede** abroad — over-index 1.13, but lost 2.12pp vs Velichie there.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 4.35% in the 138 sections at over-index 1.35 — above proportional. Fakulteta (10 sections, Sofia) gave 11.93%, Stolipinovo 4.19%, Maksuda 2.79%. Minimal change vs October 2024 (-0.58pp) — stable but small base. Not a road to 4%.

## Candidates and preferences

38,905 preferences, rate 37.23%, top-1 share 6.58%. Radostin Vasilev leads in two MIRs: 25-MIR Sofia (2,561) and Plovdiv (2,127). Hristo Rastashki took 1,313 in 23-MIR Sofia. Nikolay Radulov 968 in Varna. Kiril Veselinski 887 in Blagoevgrad. Only 1 ballot-order upset — the central list is accepted, but the bench is thin outside Vasilev.

## Competitive geography

Against Velichie: 17 won, 15 lost — essentially a tie. Top margins: Montana +2.42pp, Vratsa +2.11, 25-MIR +1.70. Losses: Abroad -2.12, Veliko Tarnovo -1.80, Silistra -1.36. The two parties split the same pool; neither crosses 4% without absorbing the other.

## Polling intelligence

Agencies were close: SH -0.03pp, CAM +0.24, MY +0.27, GIB -0.32, AR -0.43, TR +0.47, ML -0.88. No serious drift — all seven within ±1pp. For a party right on the threshold edge, that is good news — the campaign knew exactly how close, and exactly how far.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Negotiate a coalition with Velichie.** MECh + Velichie = 6.33% — cleanly over the threshold. Standalone, both under 4%.
- **Develop the north-west.** The only regions with positive deltas. Local candidates, local visibility, engagement.
- **Build a bench beyond Radostin Vasilev.** 1 upset means nobody else brings their own vote. Two cycles without party growth and this is an existential risk.
- **Strengthen presence in big cities.** Over-indexes 1.02 in Sofia and 0.99 in other big cities — close to proportional. With system this can grow.
- **Don't rely on Roma sections.** Over-index 1.35 looks attractive, but absolute votes are under 1,500 — not material.

### БСП – ОБЕДИНЕНА ЛЕВИЦА (БСП-ОЛ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9F-%D0%9E%D0%9B

## Headline result

BSP-UL (BSP-UL – United Left) took 97,753 votes (3.02%) from eighth place in its debut coalition format. This is the first time in modern Bulgarian history that a BSP-successor party is below the 4% threshold and out of parliament. Regional drops vs the prior cycle, measured against the consolidated party list, range from -2 to -4.4pp.

## What worked

- A national-map presence preserved — the party did not vanish despite structural erosion.
- A modest result in Sofia City: over-index 1.05, share 3.18% — the only place where BSP-UL is above proportional. The capital's class electorate held.
- 4 ballot-order upsets — a bench with local pull: Mincho Kazandzhiev in Lovech (520 vs 302), Todor Atanasov in Targovishte, Pavel Karaivanov in Shumen, Genadi Tsitlakidis in Gabrovo. Regional leftists with their own vote.
- Gergana Ormanlieva in Blagoevgrad — top-1 candidate with 4.73% of national preferences.
- GIB nearly exact (+0.11pp error) — for a threshold-edge party, at least one pollster delivered the true value.

## What didn't work

- Below 4%. BSP is out of parliament for the first time in history. An institutional catastrophe.
- Heavy losses in north-central regions: Pleven -4.39pp, Targovishte -4.36, prov. Plovdiv -4.14, Pazardzhik -4.00, Kyustendil -3.70. Small towns historically left-leaning turned to PB.
- Abroad over-index 0.31 — essentially no diaspora support. That is an urban-western trend and BSP-UL has no channels.
- Risk-section share — 2.03% (over-index 0.67) — under-indexed. Not a traditional field but also not a new reserve.
- Against Velichie (closest rival): won 18 of 32, lost 14 — the winning side, but no parliamentary bonus.
- Pollsters systematically overestimated: CAM +2.25pp, SH +1.58, AR +0.98, MY +0.98, TR +0.98 — only ML (-0.67) and GIB (+0.11) were close. The campaign expected 4-4.5%; reality was 3.02%.

## Geographic strategy

For a party out of parliament, geographic strategy shifts to survival. **Defend** Lovech, Kyustendil, Sofia region — the only regions with positive margins over Velichie. **Rebuild** Pleven, Targovishte, prov. Plovdiv, Pazardzhik — where 4pp packet drops are most painful. **Concede** abroad and Kardzhali (over-index under 0.4) — no return there.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 2.03% at over-index 0.67 — below proportional. Stolipinovo 2.43%, Maksuda 1.76%, Dolno Ezerovo 1.79%. BSP historically held a share of these communities; not anymore. PB took the bloc at 50%+.

## Candidates and preferences

42,740 preferences, rate 43.72% (high for a small party), top-1 4.73%. Gergana Ormanlieva leads in Blagoevgrad (2,021), Krum Zarkov in 24-MIR (1,421) and Burgas (721), Tatyana Doncheva in Plovdiv (1,121), Gabriel Valkov in 23-MIR (884). 4 ballot-order upsets — Kazandzhiev beat Berievski in Lovech 520-302; Karaivanov beat Jablianov (party leader!) in Shumen 309-177. Another signal that central names are weaker than regional ones.

## Competitive geography

Against Velichie: 18 won, 14 lost. Top margins: Yambol +2.60pp, Kyustendil +1.64, Sofia region +1.43. Losses: Abroad -4.86, Varna -1.93, Veliko Tarnovo -1.19. Small central and southern regions are better terrain for BSP-UL than the cities.

## Polling intelligence

Agencies trended mostly positive: GIB +0.11pp (nearly exact), ML -0.67, AR +0.98, MY +0.98, TR +0.98, SH +1.58, CAM +2.25. Mild systematic 1pp overestimate — five agencies had BSP-UL +1 to +2pp above the actual. The campaign expected to clear the threshold; missed by 1pp.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Decide on unification or new identity.** BSP-UL outside parliament means the coalition format must be reconsidered. Atanas Zafirov and the leadership must choose — traditional BSP or a new left.
- **Develop the regional faces.** Kazandzhiev, Karaivanov, Tsitlakidis — local networks with their own electorate. The central list does not work.
- **Defend urban class voting.** Sofia City over-index 1.05 — only there does BSP-UL have a proportional electorate above national.
- **Distrust the polls.** Systematic 1-1.5pp overestimate — next campaign must mark down and manage internal expectations.
- **Consider an alliance with PP-DB or PB.** For a party out of parliament, going alone is more expensive than concession. BSP-UL + PB on a joint list in specific MIRs may be electorally rational.

### КОАЛИЦИЯ ПРОДЪЛЖАВАМЕ ПРОМЯНАТА – ДЕМОКРАТИЧНА БЪЛГАРИЯ (ПП-ДБ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%9F%D0%9F-%D0%94%D0%91

## Headline result

PP-DB took 408,846 votes (12.62%) and slid to third — behind PB (44.59%) and GERB-SDS (13.39%) — from second with 14.21% in October 2024. The paradox: vote share fell 1.60pp but absolute votes ROSE by 62,772 in a +12pp turnout election. The urban base deepened; the national space realigned around PB.

## What worked

- The three Sofia MIRs delivered the strongest gains: 23-MIR +6.44pp (to 31.52%), 24-MIR +5.05pp (to 26.50%), 25-MIR +3.51pp (to 17.70%). The urban liberal vote consolidated.
- Abroad +6.80pp (to 22.84%) — the diaspora moved to PP-DB against the general PB tide. Abroad delivers 10.43% of the party's national vote.
- Over-index 2.06 in Sofia City and 1.81 abroad — PP-DB is the urban liberal brand by definition, no ambiguity.
- Machine voting 76.07% — the highest paper-machine inversion in the field, reflecting a young / urban / tech-literate electorate.
- 186,123 preferential votes (rate 45.52%, one of the highest) with 11 ballot-order upsets — Bozhidar Bozhanov beat Nikolay Denkov in 23-MIR Sofia (13,528 vs 9,640), Anna Bodakova beat Ivaylo Mirchev in 24-MIR, Stela Nikolova beat Pavel Popov in Varna. The bench has its own pull, not just the central list.
- Pollsters were close (errors -1.42 to +2.35pp); the campaign worked with realistic expectations.

## What didn't work

- Concentration is extreme: 56.18% of the national vote comes from 5 regions and 65.32% from 25 municipalities. PP-DB is essentially absent across most of the country.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster: over-index 0.55, share 6.91%. The party has no bridge to these communities.
- In risk neighborhoods — share 11.37% (over-index 0.90), almost unchanged from 11.83% in October 2024. PB now holds Stolipinovo at 50%; PP-DB cannot compete for that electorate.
- Against GERB-SDS: lost 26 of 32 regions; won only 6 (the three Sofia MIRs, abroad, Plovdiv-city, 25-MIR by a thin margin). Outside the urban liberal core, GERB-SDS leads by double digits: Lovech -13.52pp, Montana -12.33pp, Blagoevgrad -11.88pp.
- Vote-share losses in small conservative-leaning regions: Smolyan -2.06pp, Silistra -0.94pp, Haskovo -0.62pp. Erosion at the periphery.

## Geographic strategy

PP-DB is a party of Sofia, the diaspora and the big cities — full stop. **Defend** the three Sofia MIRs, abroad and Plovdiv-city — where the party leads or is close. **Concede** central-west and northern Bulgaria (Lovech, Montana, Vratsa) — losses there run double-digit and are not quickly recoverable. **Experiment** in Burgas (8.72%) and Varna (13.12%) — both index below what a 12.62% national party should hold in those urban markets.

## Risk neighborhoods

PP-DB took 11.37% in the 138 monitored sections, over-index 0.90 — close to the national share. Stolipinovo gave 11.81%, Maksuda 13.09%, Filipovci 16.18%. Change vs October 2024: only -0.46pp. PP-DB did not lose ground here but had no operation to capture it either. PB took 50%+ of these sections.

## Candidates and preferences

High engagement: 45.52% of voters cast a preference. The top candidate — Bozhidar Bozhanov (former e-government minister) — took 13,528 preferences in 23-MIR Sofia (7.27% of national party prefs), beating former PM Nikolay Denkov (9,640). Politically significant: PP-DB voters preferred the technocrat over the party leader. Other key names: Elisaveta Belobradova (9,864 in 23-MIR), Anna Bodakova (6,843 in 24-MIR, beating Ivaylo Mirchev), Aleksandar Simidchiev (4,531 in 25-MIR, beating Boyko Rashkov). 11 ballot-order upsets means the bench has its own electoral standing.

## Competitive geography

Against GERB-SDS (closest national rival): won 6 of 32 regions, lost 26. The wins are almost all urban-liberal: 23-MIR +19.03pp, abroad +18.17pp, 24-MIR +13.05pp, 25-MIR +3.57pp, Plovdiv-city +3.25pp. The losses span a wide periphery: Lovech -13.52pp, Montana -12.33pp, Blagoevgrad -11.88pp — a belt where PP-DB has no organisational presence.

## Polling intelligence

Agencies were close on PP-DB: ML +0.56pp, AR -1.02, SH -1.02, GIB -1.19, MY -1.22, TR -1.42, CAM +2.35. Six agencies mildly under-polled by 1-1.5pp; only CAM over-polled, at +2.35. Far less drift than for PB (-4 to -15pp) or GERB-SDS (+5 to +11pp). The campaign's polling picture was credible.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Accept the identity and invest in it.** PP-DB is the urban liberal alternative to PB. Trim national ambitions in favour of depth in Sofia, abroad and the big cities.
- **Promote Bozhanov and the next generation.** The 11 ballot-order upsets show the electorate rewards individual figures over party leaders. Use it.
- **Don't chase the ethnic-mixed cluster.** Over-index 0.55 at national-campaign cost is negative ROI. Cede those regions to the DPS-APS family and PB.
- **Prepare for the next contest against PB, not GERB-SDS.** In 23-MIR and 24-MIR, PB is now the principal rival. The 2026 strategy aimed at GERB-SDS became obsolete on April 19.
- **Defend abroad aggressively.** +6.80pp in the diaspora at +0.81 national activity there is a strong result — but PB took 38% there. It will be attacked.

### ВЪЗРАЖДАНЕ (Възраждане)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%92%D1%8A%D0%B7%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5

## Headline result

Vazrazhdane took 137,940 votes (4.26%) and barely cleared the 4% threshold from fifth place — down from 13.36% in October 2024 (third position), a -9.11pp loss and -187,418 votes. One of the largest losses in the field: Kostadinov's party held parliamentary presence at the cost of two-thirds of its electorate.

## What worked

- Cleared the threshold. Given the depth of the collapse, that is a political victory in itself — preserves the structure for the next cycle.
- Abroad over-index 1.23 — the diaspora stayed proportionally stronger than the national average. 7.10% of the party vote comes from abroad, more than from several larger parties.
- Kostadinov held the facade: 5.29% of national prefs, leader in Varna (2,568) and 25-MIR Sofia (2,476). For a party in free fall, the leader stayed recognisable.
- Polling agencies overestimated the party by 1-4pp — the campaign entered the day expecting 5-8%; reality was 4.26%, but not a catastrophe.

## What didn't work

- A -9.11pp loss and -187,418 votes in a +12pp turnout election — new voters did not appear for the nationalist option; old ones left.
- Heavy drops in central and eastern Bulgaria: Yambol -7.67pp, Stara Zagora -7.45, Dobrich -7.13, Veliko Tarnovo -7.02, Gabrovo -6.94. The party collapsed in its own strongholds.
- Risk-section share fell from 13.81% to 4.84% (-8.97pp) — Vazrazhdane also held a slice of the Roma sections; it transferred to PB.
- 0 ballot-order upsets out of 30 — total dominance of the central list. When Kostadinov loses, the party has no local figures with their own votes to take the relay.
- Against new competition from MECh (close in ideology): won only 29 of 32 regions, but with minimal margins — Varna +3.19pp, Veliko Tarnovo +1.81, Dobrich +1.81. That is not a safe lead; it is MECh's breakthrough everywhere.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** the 4% threshold above everything else. **Rebuild** in central-east Bulgaria (Yambol, Stara Zagora, Dobrich), where the party lost 7pp in a single cycle. **Concede** the urban national-conservative space to MECh and Siyanie — they are growing from a low base but the count keeps rising.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share fell from 13.81% to 4.84%, a -8.97pp drop — almost identical to DPS's. The over-index stays at 1.14 (slightly over-indexed), but the absolute votes transferred to PB. Maksuda (Varna) gave 6.43%, Stolipinovo 4.29%, Dolno Ezerovo 5.32%. Vazrazhdane has no field operation to rebuild this base.

## Candidates and preferences

48,545 preferences, rate 35.19%, top-1 share 5.29% — concentrated around Kostadinov. He leads in two MIRs: Varna (2,568) and 25-MIR Sofia (2,476). Tsoncho Ganev — the party's #2 — takes 1,825 in 23-MIR Sofia and 1,180 in Burgas. Iskra Mihaylova in Stara Zagora (1,234) — the only female face in the top 5. Zero ballot-order upsets means the central list is absolute, but also that the party has no bench to succeed the leader.

## Competitive geography

Against MECh (closest rival): won 29 of 32, lost 3. Top margins: Varna +3.19pp, Veliko Tarnovo +1.81, Dobrich +1.81. Losses: Vratsa -0.86pp, Lovech -0.51, Pleven -0.37. The thin margins show MECh is the real threat next cycle — one wobble and Vazrazhdane could fall out.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies overestimated the party: ML +0.68pp, AR +1.54, GIB +2.54, TR +2.84, MY +3.14, SH +3.74, CAM +4.48. Systematic 1-4pp inflation — the campaign expected 6-8%. The polling model captured stated support but not actual late-cycle voting for the nationalist option, which clearly collapsed in the final weeks — votes that PB absorbed.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Build a bench beyond Kostadinov.** Zero upsets at -9pp collapse means there is no successor. If Kostadinov steps back, the party drops to 1-2%.
- **Defend the 4% line with a focused campaign in strongholds.** Yambol, Stara Zagora, Dobrich, V. Tarnovo — that is where the -7pp collapse was. A 2pp recovery there alone means 4.5-5% nationally.
- **Distrust the polls.** Systematic 2-4pp overestimate — next campaign must mark down and manage expectations.
- **Accept the Roma-share loss.** Recovery against 50%+ PB is expensive. Better to segment: national-conservative votes in small towns.
- **Consider a coalition with MECh or Siyanie.** The three parties combined are 10.50% — solid parliamentary weight. Standalone, each is under 5%.

## Polling — per-agency analysis

### Alpha Research

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/AR
Website: https://alpharesearch.bg/

**Summary:** Alpha Research leads the industry-bias-adjusted, shrunken leaderboard (shrunkAdj=0.51) with 5 elections covered. Raw MAE 1.60 is the lowest in the system. AR is the only major agency that publishes a forecast among decided voters (already redistributed), so the analyzer scores it as-is — no normalisation applied. Median fieldwork 5 days before vote; +0.10 plus-minus puts AR slightly ahead of cross-agency consensus.

**Bias profile:** Mild pro-establishment fingerprint: overpolls ГЕРБ-СДС (+1.54pp across 5 cycles) and БСП-ОЛ (+1.40pp across 5 cycles). Reformist bloc systematically underpolled (-2.64pp across 5 cycles). The strongest non-2026 single miss is БСП +4.79pp in April 2021 — when every house overpolled БСП.

**Warning:** Only 5 cycles — 2017 and earlier are not covered. AR's 2024-06-09 record corrected on 2026-05-19 after a missing 5-day-before final wave was added (the Wikipedia scrape had only picked up the agency's March 2024 wave, 98 days before vote); the cycle MAE dropped from 2.94 to 1.14 once the actual final poll was loaded. The 2026 ПрБ miss (-10.39pp) tracks the cross-agency pattern.

### Trend

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/TR
Website: https://rc-trend.bg/

**Summary:** Trend ranks second by shrunkAdj (0.59) with the longest active history in the dataset — 9 elections from 2017 to 2026. Raw MAE 1.62 is second-lowest, behind AR's 1.60. Trend is consistently a late-fieldwork pollster (median 5 days before vote) and posted a 93% barrier-call rate — among the highest in the system, edged only by Gallup's 94%.

**Bias profile:** Notable underpoll of the reformist bloc (-3.48pp across 7 cycles) and ПП specifically (-7.33pp across the 2021-11 and 2022-10 debut cycles). +0.19pp plus-minus signals a slight tendency to beat cross-agency consensus.

**Warning:** The 2026 ПрБ miss (-11.39pp) is Trend's worst single-party error and pulled the cycle MAE to 2.51 despite 3-day fieldwork — a cross-agency blind spot, not a TR-specific signature.

### Gallup Intl. Balkan

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/GIB
Website: https://www.gallup-international.bg/

**Summary:** Gallup ranks third by shrunkAdj (0.62) with 7 elections spanning 2021-04 to 2026-04 — the third-longest record in the dataset (after Trend's 9 and Market Links's 8). Raw MAE 2.04, barrier-call rate 94% (highest in the system), median fieldwork 5 days before vote.

**Bias profile:** Mild establishment lean — БСП-ОЛ +1.97pp across 7 cycles, ГЕРБ-СДС +1.74pp across 7. Reformist bloc systematically underpolled (-4.39pp across 6 cycles — the deepest sustained reformist underpoll in the dataset).

**Warning:** The 2026 ПрБ miss (-14.71pp) is the largest single-party error in the entire dataset — Gallup's 20-day-old fieldwork was the latest among 2026 final polls, and the late ПрБ wave hit it hardest. The 2021-11 ПП miss (-10.17pp) shows the same blind spot for late-rising parties.

### Sova Harris

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/SH
Website: https://sovaharris.com/

**Summary:** Sova Harris ranks fourth by shrunkAdj (0.67) with 6 elections covered. Raw MAE 1.66, second-lowest among the four long-history agencies (TR 1.62, ML 1.67, GIB 2.04). Median fieldwork 10 days before vote — slightly later than the front-runners, which costs accuracy in cycles with late-breaking party movements. +0.05 plus-minus is the most neutral direction among all 8 agencies.

**Bias profile:** Mild left tilt: БСП-ОЛ +1.97pp across 7 cycles. ИТН consistently underpolled (-2.36pp across 5 cycles). Reformist bloc -2.28pp underpoll across 5 cycles. ДБ specifically -3.34pp across 2 cycles (2021-04 and 2021-07).

**Warning:** Sample sizes (typically n=800-1000) sit at the lower end of reliable polling. The 2026 ПрБ miss (-10.99pp) is SH's largest single-party error. SH's 2023-04-02 record was corrected on 2026-05-19 after a missing 9-day-before final wave was added (cycle MAE dropped from 1.97 to 1.02).

### Myara

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/MY
Website: https://myara.bg/

**Summary:** Myara is a young agency — only the April 2026 cycle is in the dataset. shrunkAdj 0.70 (provisional given n=1). Raw MAE 2.30 with 6-day fieldwork. The shrinkage prior gives Myara reasonable benefit-of-the-doubt early on, but a single-cycle profile cannot separate house effect from cycle-specific accident. Agency website (myara.bg) was launched in late 2024.

**Bias profile:** Single-election sample. 2026 errors mirror the cross-agency pattern: ПрБ -9.99pp, ГЕРБ-СДС +5.11pp, Възраждане +3.14pp. +0.25pp plus-minus.

**Warning:** Profile is provisional. Wait for 2-3 more cycles before drawing conclusions about house effect — at n=1 the line between methodology and cycle accident cannot be drawn.

### Center for Analysis and Marketing

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/CAM

**Summary:** CAM (Center for Analysis and Marketing) is a new entrant with one election in the dataset (2026). Raw MAE 2.75, shrunkAdj 0.95 — grade A. Fieldwork closed 5 days before vote — competitive timing, but with the second-largest ГЕРБ-СДС overpoll in the cycle (Gallup at 20 days posted +11.21pp).

**Bias profile:** Single-election sample. 2026 errors: ГЕРБ-СДС +9.88pp (second-largest single-party overpoll in the cycle, after Gallup's +11.21pp), ДПС +6.32pp, ПрБ -6.08pp (smallest ПрБ miss in 2026 alongside ML). -0.28pp plus-minus.

**Warning:** Profile is provisional — wait for 2-3 more cycles. The agency has no agency-domain website; both 2026 polls are locked via third-party press consensus (banker.bg, actualno.com, dnes.dir.bg, epicenter.bg, eurocom.bg).

### Mediana

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/MD

**Summary:** Mediana ranks seventh with only 2 elections in the system. Raw MAE 3.24, shrunkAdj 0.96 — shrinkage caps small-sample agencies near the neutral floor. Both Mediana cycles (2021-11 and 2024-10) show large bias. Mediana's primary domain (mediana.bg) is parked on sedo.com, so all MD polls are locked via third-party consensus (Trud, Wikipedia citations).

**Bias profile:** Strongest left tilt in the system: БСП +4.36pp average (n=2) — the largest single-party bias in the dataset. ГЕРБ-СДС also overpolled (+3.36pp average). Plus-minus -1.05 — pattern of underpolling the winning side.

**Warning:** Two-cycle sample is insufficient for confident bias estimates. Lowest barrier-call rate in the system (80%) — Mediana made the most wrong in/out calls per cycle.

### Market Links

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/polls/ML
Website: https://www.marketlinks.bg/

**Summary:** Market Links has the third-lowest raw MAE in the dataset (1.67, behind AR's 1.60 and Trend's 1.62) and the second-deepest active history (8 elections, behind Trend's 9), but ranks last among A+ agencies by shrunkAdj (0.97). The gap reflects house style: ML publishes raw electoral attitudes with an explicit undecided share, and the analyzer's mechanical redistribution doesn't fully neutralize the bloc-level lean visible across cycles. Across the 2025-2026 mid-cycle waves, ML moved to publishing the agency's own "Voting" column directly — preserved as-is during validation.

**Bias profile:** Mild left tilt — БСП-ОЛ +2.07pp across 8 cycles. House effect of +1.46pp on the right-government bloc and -1.32pp on the populist bloc. No single bloc-level lean exceeds 2.1pp — narrower than Gallup's reformist underpoll (-4.4pp) or Trend's (-3.5pp).

**Warning:** ML's cycle MAE 1.76 was the best in the 2026 field. On the ПрБ axis specifically, ML (-6.59pp) and CAM (-6.08pp) were the two closest, with the other five agencies 10+pp short. In 2021-11 the cycle-final poll missed ПП by -8.01pp; older mid-cycle waves should be read with timing in mind.

# Following the public money: a citizen's toolkit for procurement

Bulgaria signs tens of thousands of public-procurement contracts a year. The records are public — and almost unusable. They live as thousands of files on [data.egov.bg](https://data.egov.bg/) and inside the [ЦАИС ЕОП](https://app.eop.bg/) system, with no way to ask the questions that matter: *Who keeps winning without competition? Which companies are tied to the people who run the state? Where does my município's money go?*

The [Public Procurement](/procurement) module answers those questions. It holds **301,011 contracts and amendments** worth **€80.0 billion**, from **4,389 contracting authorities** to **26,160 companies**, covering **2011 through 2026** — and it layers an explainable risk score, money-flow diagrams, a person scanner, a geographic view, sector (CPV) breakdowns, a contracts browser with sector/procedure/value/EU-funding filters, and a red-flag feed on top. This piece sets it against what exists in Bulgaria and abroad, walks through each tool, and ends with what you can actually find with it.

## 1. The landscape: Bulgaria and abroad

**In Bulgaria,** the primary source is the Public Procurement Agency (АОП) and the ЦАИС ЕОП platform, republished as open data on [data.egov.bg](https://data.egov.bg/organisation/about/aop). It is comprehensive and authoritative — and raw: no analytics, no risk scoring, and crucially no link between a contract and the *people* behind the winning company. In June 2026 the Ministry of Innovation and Digital Transformation launched [СИГМА](https://sigma.midt.bg) (sigma.midt.bg), a government analytics layer over the *same* АОП data. It has a clean interface and ships a working browser of authorities, companies and contracts — with filters by sector (CPV), procedure type, year, value and EU funding, search by name, EIK or contract number, sector-level money-flow diagrams, and CSV download of any list (and JSON for a single contract) — from day one, a solid base to build on. The more ambitious features it announced (an AI assistant, a green/yellow/red risk index, red-flag signals and a beneficial-owner layer) are, for now, slated for a later stage.

Beyond the official registers, Bulgaria has accumulated civic and commercial efforts around procurement — from investigative journalism to business services:

| Platform | What it is | Focus | Status |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [BIRD / Bivol](https://scan.bird.bg/) | investigative journalism + search | PEPs, public spending, companies, procurement, EU funds — search by name | active |
| [IME — Open Public Procurement](https://ime.bg/) | open-data analysis + a dedicated site (oop.ime.bg) | spending efficiency, indicators | the dedicated site is no longer maintained |
| [Anti-Corruption Fund](https://acf.bg/) | investigative NGO | specific procurement schemes — reports, not a database | active |
| [BILI](http://www.bili-bg.org/) | legal-initiatives NGO | integrity, declarations, judicial transparency (not a procurement tool) | active |
| [aop-baza.bg](https://www.aop-baza.bg/), [targove.info](https://www.targove.info/) | commercial alert services | subscription: filtered BG+EU notices, daily email (free trial) | active · paid |
| [ZOP Plus](https://zopplus.com/) | specialist magazine + "ZOP+ Assistant" | expert consulting, training, documentation | active · paid |

**Abroad,** the reference standard is the [Open Contracting Data Standard](https://standard.open-contracting.org/) (OCDS), which makes procurement comparable across countries. The EU-wide [opentender.eu](https://opentender.eu/) project (DIGIWHIST) pioneered a quantitative **Corruption Risk Index** — the work of Mihály Fazekas and the [Government Transparency Institute](https://www.govtransparency.eu/) — built on objective red flags: single bidding, short tender windows, non-open procedures, supplier concentration. Ukraine pairs its [ProZorro](https://prozorro.gov.ua/) procurement system with the civil-society [DOZORRO](https://dozorro.org/) layer, which monitors risk and lets anyone *follow* a buyer or supplier. Commercial platforms (Spend Network and Tussell in the UK, GovSpend in the US) sell buyer/supplier dashboards and alerts; the US [USAspending.gov](https://www.usaspending.gov/) offers a drill-down explorer with geographic maps.

**Where this module fits:** it borrows the international playbook — the explainable Fazekas-style risk index, the DOZORRO "follow an entity" idea, OCDS-grade structure — and adds the one thing none of the others localise: the **political-accountability cross-join**. Every contract is checked against the Bulgarian political class — MPs, ministers, agency heads, governors, mayors, deputy-mayors and councillors — via their declarations to the [Audit Office](https://register.cacbg.bg/) and the [Commerce Registry](https://portal.registryagency.bg/CR/). The table below compares feature by feature.

| Feature | АОП / ЦАИС ЕОП | SIGMA | opentender.eu | ProZorro / DOZORRO | Naiasno |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Coverage | all PPA contracts | 2020– | EU, incl. BG | Ukraine | BG, 2011–2026 |
| Open standard (OCDS) | yes | no | yes | yes | yes |
| Explainable risk index | no | announced | yes | yes | yes |
| Single-bidder flag | no | partial | yes | yes | yes |
| Other red flags | no | announced | yes | yes | yes |
| Money-flow diagrams | no | yes | no | partial | yes |
| Filter by sector / value / procedure | no | yes | yes | yes | yes |
| Links to politicians / owners | no | announced | no | partial | yes |
| Map by region / municipality | no | no | partial | yes | yes |
| Search by person / company | partial | yes | yes | yes | yes |
| Follow / watchlist | no | no | no | yes | yes |
| AI assistant (natural language) | no | announced | no | partial | yes |
| Local-government procurement | no | partial | partial | yes | yes |
| Access | free · state | free · state | free · academic | free · state + civic | free · Bulgarian · independent |

"Announced" means a feature stated on the roadmap but not yet shipped (as of June 2026).

A second group sits outside this comparison: commercial market-intelligence platforms and public-spending portals. They solve a different problem — helping vendors win customers, or making one government's spending visible — so they don't score corruption risk or link contracts to politicians:

| Platform | What it is | For whom / focus | Access |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| [Spend Network](https://www.spendnetwork.com/) | global procurement database (160+ countries) | suppliers & analysts | paid |
| [Tussell](https://www.tussell.com/) | UK contract & framework data | supplier market intelligence | paid |
| [GovSpend](https://govspend.com/) | US procurement & spend data | selling to the public sector | paid |
| [USAspending.gov](https://www.usaspending.gov/) | official US federal spending portal | government-spending transparency | free · state |

## 2. The tools

### An explainable risk index, not a black box

Every contract carries a **Corruption Risk Index** from 0 to 100 — the share of the applicable red-flag checks that fired, in the Fazekas/Government-Transparency-Institute tradition. It is deliberately transparent: the page shows *which* checks fired and how many were even applicable ("3 of 7 risk checks"), so you can judge it yourself rather than trust a colour.

![A contract page with the explainable Corruption Risk Index meter and red-flag chips](/articles/images/procurement-tools/01-risk-index.png)

*[See it live: an example contract →](/procurement/contract/701291266900)*

The checks: a **single bidder** (read from the bid count the OCDS feed actually publishes, and suppressed in markets that are structurally single-bid so it doesn't cry wolf[^cpv]), a **non-open procedure**, a **short tender window**, an **amendment** that revises the original deal, a contractor on the АОП **debarment register**, a buyer whose spending is **concentrated** on one supplier, and a contractor **tied to an MP or a public official**.

### Where the money flows

Each company and authority page draws the money flow as a Sankey diagram — for a supplier, which authorities pay it; for a buyer, which suppliers it pays — with companies tied to a parliamentarian highlighted.

![A buyer-to-supplier money-flow Sankey diagram on a company page](/articles/images/procurement-tools/02-entity-flow.png)

*[See it live: a company page →](/company/103267194)*

A treemap shows the same composition by size, so concentration is visible at a glance.

![A treemap of a company's procurement revenue by buyer](/articles/images/procurement-tools/03-treemap.png)

*[See it live: a company page →](/company/103267194)*

### The people behind the companies

The module surfaces, on each company page, the politicians tied to it — and not only MPs. Mayors, deputy-mayors, councillors, ministers, governors and agency heads are matched to the companies they declared a stake in or appear as an officer of in the Commerce Registry.

![The "connected officials" section on a company page](/articles/images/procurement-tools/04-officials.png)

*[See it live: a company page →](/company/202758921)*

Or start from the person: the [public money scanner](/procurement/people) lets you type a politician and see the procurement reachable through their connected companies.

![The public money scanner, searching a politician by procurement ties](/articles/images/procurement-tools/07-scanner.png)

*[See it live: the public money scanner →](/procurement/people)*

A link here is a **declared tie from a public register, not an accusation**. Bulgarian law lets officials own shares; it forbids sitting MPs from management roles but not past business or ownership. The tool surfaces the relationship and cites the source — the judgement is yours.

### Your own município

Local procurement surfaces on every place dashboard: what the município, its schools and its hospitals spent, and on whom.

![The local-procurement tile on a place dashboard](/articles/images/procurement-tools/08-myarea.png)

*[See it live: the Plovdiv dashboard →](/governance/PDV22)*

And the [maps](/procurement/by-settlement) show every oblast three ways at once — total, **per capita** (so they don't just redraw the population map) and average contract value. Click any oblast on any of the maps to filter the settlement table beneath them.

![Choropleth maps of procurement by oblast — total, per capita and average contract value](/articles/images/procurement-tools/05-choropleth.png)

*[See it live: the oblast maps →](/procurement/by-settlement)*

### The red-flag feed

The [red-flag feed](/procurement/flags) collects the signals worth a second look in one place — buyers concentrated on a single supplier, active debarments, and the largest politically-connected contractors. And, DOZORRO-style, you can **follow** any buyer, supplier or politician and keep them on your own watchlist.

![The procurement red-flag feed](/articles/images/procurement-tools/06-flags.png)

*[See it live: the red-flag feed →](/procurement/flags)*

## 3. What you can find

**Single-supplier concentration.** Across the corpus, **45% of contracts whose bid count is published had a single bidder** — Bulgaria's well-documented competition problem. The feed surfaces the extreme cases: buyers that have sent *100%* of their procurement to one company — often small schools and community centres. And sometimes the scale surprises: a secondary school in the village of Ribnovo placed a single **€2.5 million** contract with one Blagoevgrad firm — roughly 95% of everything it has ever awarded. Even if each award was lawful, that degree of concentration warrants closer scrutiny.

**The political class as contractors.** The module records **61 MPs tied to 64 companies** that have won contracts worth **€1.4 billion** over the full period, and **82 non-MP officials** tied to **81** contractor companies. The largest ties run through state-owned enterprises: an MP registered as a director of the state road-builder [Avtomagistrali](/company/831646048) — **€602 million** in contracts; another MP at [Bulgarian Posts](/company/121396123) at **€182 million**; a state-agency head registered at the IT company [Informatsionno Obsluzhvane](/company/831641791) at **€315 million**. Alongside them are municipal councillors with a directly declared stake — e.g. in [Global Cleaner](/company/202758921) (cleaning, €25 million) and [Etropal Trade](/company/122055819) (medical supplies, €13 million). None of this is itself wrongdoing — it is exactly the map of declared interest that was, until now, scattered across thousands of filings.

**Per-município reality.** Because every local buyer is pinned to its settlement, you can read a município like [Plovdiv](/procurement/settlement/56784) directly: **€3.9 billion** awarded across 15,286 contracts, led by the university hospital, the regional electricity distributor and the municipality itself.

## 4. Method and limits

All of these features rest on the same open АОП / ЦАИС ЕОП data — no private source. The links to politicians add only two further official public registers: the asset-and-interest declarations to the Court of Audit and the Commerce Registry. The single-bidder signal reads the realised bid count the OCDS feed publishes; it is gated against a per-sector competition baseline so structurally single-bid markets aren't falsely flagged. Person links use **only** high-confidence matches — a declared stake or a unique-name Commerce-Registry record — and are dropped where a common Bulgarian name would create false positives. Out of scope: contracts below the Public Procurement Act thresholds, in-house awards, and foreign suppliers. The risk index is a sorting and screening aid, not legal evidence; every figure links back to its source on data.egov.bg so you can check it yourself.

Open the [Public Procurement](/procurement) module, or ask the [assistant](https://ai.electionsbg.com) a question like *"show the procurement red flags"* — and follow the money.

- Fazekas, Tóth & King — *Anatomy of Grand Corruption: A Composite Corruption Risk Index Based on Objective Data* (SSRN): [papers.ssrn.com/abstract=2331980](https://papers.ssrn.com/abstract=2331980)

**International tools**

- opentender.eu (DIGIWHIST): [opentender.eu](https://opentender.eu/)
- ProZorro (Ukraine): [prozorro.gov.ua](https://prozorro.gov.ua/)
- DOZORRO (Transparency International Ukraine): [dozorro.org](https://dozorro.org/)
- Spend Network: [spendnetwork.com](https://www.spendnetwork.com/)
- Tussell: [tussell.com](https://www.tussell.com/)
- GovSpend: [govspend.com](https://govspend.com/)
- USAspending.gov: [usaspending.gov](https://www.usaspending.gov/)

[^cpv]: We decide this per sector, from the data — no hand-picked list. For each two-digit CPV division (the EU's Common Procurement Vocabulary) we measure the share of contracts with a published bid count that had only one bidder; if that share is 80% or more, we treat the division as structurally single-bid and suppress the flag there. The thresholds are recomputed from the corpus on every update. Currently 7 of 45 divisions qualify — among them water supply, electricity/gas/water distribution, postal and telecom services, real estate, R&D services, and printed matter.

### How the budget simulator works: data and model
